## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / nonlinear dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form for (non)linear oscillators. Common relationships combine a restoring force term in x, damping terms in v, and optional external/parametric forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator (SHO): dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hooke-law restoring force, conservative)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper)
- Quadratic/nonlinear drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (high-Re drag / nonlinear dissipation)
- Coulomb (dry) friction approximation: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v / sqrt(v**2 + c2) (velocity-sign-like friction with smoothing)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Higher-order odd restoring force: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (symmetric nonlinear spring expansions)
- Simple pendulum (nonlinear sine restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (large-angle pendulum with damping)
- Externally forced oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven vibration / resonance)
- Duffing with forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear resonance, bistability)
- Parametric (Mathieu-type) excitation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness, parametric resonance)
- Van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillation / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excitation via nonlinear dissipation)
- Conservative potential-force form (polynomial potential): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) (equivalent to motion in V(x) = c2 * x**2 + c3 * x**4)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative symmetric oscillator → dv_dt is an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x - x**3) and contains no standalone v term (energy conserved when no damping/forcing).
- Linear viscous damping → a term -c * v; it reduces amplitude without changing the restoring-force nonlinearity.
- Nonlinear stiffness/spring hardening/softening → presence of x**3 (Duffing) and higher odd powers; sign of coefficient shifts frequency with amplitude.
- Dry friction / stick-slip tendency → dv_dt contains a near-sign(v) contribution (approximated smoothly via v/sqrt(v**2+c)).
- Aerodynamic/high-Re dissipation → v * Abs(v) (or higher powers of v) appear; decay rate increases with speed.
- Self-excited limit cycles → damping depends on state, typically (1 - c * x**2) * v or (1 - c * v**2) * v, giving negative damping at small amplitude and positive at large amplitude.
- External driving → additive periodic term in t (sin/cos of c*t); enables resonance and phase locking.
- Parametric resonance → time-periodic coefficient multiplying x, e.g., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x; instability tongues occur near frequency ratios.

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v - c0*beta*v - mu*(c1 - x**c2)*v - omega0**c3*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is:
\[
F(x,t,v)=0.2647138982\,\sin t\;-\;0.3778288376\,v\sin x\;-\;0.7556576753\,v\;-\;0.7480073028\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;3.8704902421\,x e^{-|x|}.
\]
Key structural requirements for any exact match (for all real \(x,v,t\)):

1) **Must contain \(v\sin(x)\)** term (odd in \(v\), nonlinear in \(x\) via \(\sin x\)).  
2) **Must contain \(x e^{-|x|}\)** term (depends on \(|x|\); non-analytic at 0 due to absolute value).  
3) Time forcing is **pure \(\sin(t)\)** (can be represented as a cosine with phase shift).  
4) Remaining \(v\)-terms are polynomial in \(x\): \(-0.7556576753 v -0.7480073028 v +0.7480073028 v x^2\), i.e. a linear-in-\(v\) constant plus \(v x^2\).

---

### Candidates 28, 29, 31, 33, 36, 37, 39, 40, 41, 42, 45, 46, 47 (contain cos(c*log(c*exp(c*t)+1)) time-warp; no v*sin(x); no x*exp(-Abs(x)))
All of these have a highly specific time function \(\cos(c4\log(c5 e^{c6 t}+1))\), which cannot be made exactly equal to \(\sin t\) for all \(t\) by choosing constants (it is not a linear function of \(t\) except in degenerate limits, and even then not exactly). More importantly, none include \(v\sin x\) or \(x e^{-|x|}\). Cannot match any of them.

(Details: even if you set the amplitude of that term to 0 to remove it, you still don’t gain the missing \(v\sin x\) and \(x e^{-|x|}\) structures.)

---

### Candidate 44 (has v|v| and x^5; no v*sin(x); no x*exp(-Abs(x)))
44. Contains \(v|v|\) which GT does not have, and lacks both \(v\sin x\) and \(x e^{-|x|}\). Cannot match.

---

### Candidate 48 (v|v| and x*sin(t); wrong coupling)
48. Has \(x\sin(c7 t+c8)\) (time forcing multiplied by \(x\)), but GT forcing is independent of \(x\). Also has \(v|v|\) not in GT, and lacks \(v\sin x\) and \(x e^{-|x|}\). Cannot match.

---

### Candidate 49 (has v*x^2 and cos(t); still no v*sin(x), no x*exp(-Abs(x)))
49. Could match some polynomial-in-\(v\) pieces by setting many constants to 0 and tuning \(c5\) for \(v x^2\), and \(c7\cos(\cdot)\) could phase-shift to \(\sin t\). But it still lacks \(v\sin x\) and \(x e^{-|x|}\). Cannot match.

---

### Candidate 50 (x*cos(t) and v|v|; no v*sin(x); no x*exp(-Abs(x)))
50. Has \(x\cos(c4 t)\) coupling and \(v|v|\). GT has neither, and still missing \(v\sin x\) and \(x e^{-|x|}\). Cannot match.

---

### Conclusion
Every candidate lacks at least one of the two indispensable GT structures: the **state-dependent damping term** \(-\beta v\sin x\) and the **non-polynomial restoring term** \(-3.87049\,x e^{-|x|}\). Since constants cannot introduce missing functional dependence (like multiplying by \(v\), introducing \(\sin x\) inside a \(v\)-term, or creating \(x e^{-|x|}\) from polynomials or \(e^{k|x|}\) without an \(x\) factor), no candidate can be made identical to the GT for all real \(x,v,t\).

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO43)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v - c0*beta*v - mu*(c1 - x**c2)*v - omega0**c3*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.748007*v*(1 - x²) - 0.377829*v*sin(x) - 0.755658*v - 3.87049*x*exp(-|x|) + 0.264714*sin(t)`

Expanding: `0.748007*v*x² - 0.748007*v - 0.377829*v*sin(x) - 0.755658*v - 3.87049*x*exp(-|x|) + 0.264714*sin(t)`

Simplifying: `0.748007*v*x² - 1.503665*v - 0.377829*v*sin(x) - 3.87049*x*exp(-|x|) + 0.264714*sin(t)`

Key basis functions in GT:
1. `v*x²` - polynomial
2. `v` - linear in v
3. `v*sin(x)` - product of v and sin(x)
4. `x*exp(-|x|)` - product of x and exp(-|x|)
5. `sin(t)` - sinusoidal in t

Now let me analyze candidates. The critical question is whether any candidate can reproduce ALL these basis functions. The problematic terms are `v*sin(x)` and `x*exp(-|x|)`.

**Most candidates** have structures like polynomials in x and v, plus `cos(c*t + c)` for the time dependence. They typically include terms like `v`, `x`, `v*x²`, `v³`, `x³`, `x⁵`, etc. None of these polynomial terms can reproduce `v*sin(x)` or `x*exp(-|x|)` exactly (by linear independence of polynomials, exponentials, and trigonometric functions).

Let me check candidates that might have the right structure:

**Candidate 8:** `c0*v + c1*x + c2*v*x² + c3*v³ + c4*cos(c5*t + c6) + c7*sin(c8*x + c9)`
This has `sin(c8*x + c9)` but NOT `v*sin(x)` — the v multiplier is missing. Also missing `x*exp(-|x|)`. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidates 27, 32, 34:** Have `exp(c7*|c8*x|)` terms. This gives `exp(c*|x|)` which with c<0 could give `exp(-c|x|)`, but we need `x*exp(-|x|)`, not just `exp(-|x|)`. Missing the x multiplier and `v*sin(x)`. **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidates with `cos(c4*log(c5*exp(c6*t) + 1))`:** If c5 is very large, `log(c5*exp(c6*t)+1) ≈ log(c5) + c6*t`, so `cos(c4*(log(c5)+c6*t))` which is `cos(c4*c6*t + c4*log(c5))` — essentially `cos(at+b)` ≈ `sin(t)` with right constants. But this is only approximate, not exact (the "+1" can't be dropped). **[NO MATCH]** for all such candidates by Rule 2.

**Candidate 42:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v*x² + c3*v + c4*cos(c5*log(c6*exp(c7*t) + 1)) + c8*v`
Has `v*x²` and `v` terms, but the time term is approximate, missing `v*sin(x)` and `x*exp(-|x|)`. **[NO MATCH]**

After careful analysis, **no candidate** contains both `v*sin(x)` and `x*exp(-|x|)` as basis functions. These are essential components of the GT that cannot be reproduced by polynomials, and by the principle of linear independence, no polynomial combination can exactly equal these transcendental functions.
